http://creative.360yield.com/file/510/1x1.jpg :: 59 :: Peugeot :: 60 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/view-classic-cars-for-sale.php/searchtype/browse/browseby/make/browsevalue/Peugeot :: 61 :: 's flagship, the 504 made its public debut on 12 September 1968 at the Paris Salon. The press launch which had been scheduled for June 1968 was at the last minute deferred by three months, and production got off to a similarly delayed start because of the political and industrial disruption which exploded across the country in May 1968 . :: 62 :: <BR/> :: 63 :: The 504 was a sunroof-equipped four-door saloon, introduced with a carburated 1796 cc four-cylinder petrol engine 97 bhp (72 kW; 98 PS)with optional fuel injection and 82 bhp (61 kW; 83 PS) . A column-mounted four-speed manual transmission was standard, a 3-speed ZF 3HP22 automatic available as an upgrade. :: 64 :: <BR/> :: 65 :: The 504 was European Car of the Year in 1969, praised for its styling, quality, chassis, ride, visibility, strong engine and refinement. :: 66 :: <BR/> :: 67 :: The 504 Injection two-door coupé and two-door cabriolet were introduced at the Salon de Geneva in March 1969. The engine produced the same 97 bhp (72 kW; 98 PS) of output as in the fuel injected saloon, but the final drive ratio was slightly revised to give a slightly higher road speed of 20.6 mph (33.2 km/h) at 1,000 rpm. :: 68 :: <BR/> :: 69 :: The 504 received a new four-cylinder 1971 cc engine, rated at 93 bhp (carburated) and 116 bhp (fuel injected), and a four-cylinder 2112 cc diesel rated at 65 bhp (48 kW; 66 PS). The 1796 cc engine remained available. :: 70 :: <BR/> :: 71 :: In September 1970 an estate was added, featuring a higher rear roof and solid rear axle with four coil springs. It was joined by the 7-seat Familiale , which had all its occupants facing forward in three rows of seats. :: 72 :: <BR/> :: 73 :: Specifications. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 138 :: 	<BR/> :: 139 :: Some History of the Renault Caravelle :: 140 :: 1968 Renault Caravelle :: 141 :: <BR/> :: 142 :: Introduced to the UK in 1962 as the Caravelle and designed by the Italian studio Frua, this model was built for Renault by Chausson with final assembly and trim, virtually by hand, by Brissoneau and Lotz. The genius of another Italian, engineer Amde Gordini increased the output of the small Dauphine engine somewhat - the larger 1108cc R8 engines in the later Caravelle versions such as this one - producing a brisk and respectable performance, matched with all-round disc brakes. Oozing French Riviera styling, the Caravelle Convertible was not cheap at £1296 against the £582 Morris Minor Convertible - consequently attracting more affluent drivers seeking that little bit of extra style in those swinging sixties. Economy, practicality and personality are the characteristics of this overlooked and rare Sixties classic. :: 143 :: <BR/> :: 144 :: . :: 145 :: <BR/> :: 146 :: <BR/> :: 147 :: More History of the Renault Caravelle :: 148 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/115 :: 149 :: <BR/> :: 150 :: <BR/> :: 151 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 152 :: 	The classic :: 153 :: cars :: 154 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-page.php/carno/97993# :: 155 :: for :: 156 :: sale :: 157 :: http://images.intellitxt.com/ast/adTypes/mag-glass_10x10.gif :: 158 :: below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1968 Renault Caravelle Coupe for sale. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 141 :: 	<BR/> :: 142 :: Some History of the Aston Martin V8 :: 143 :: A host of improvements were to be incorporated in the forthcoming Series 4, scheduled for introduction in October 1978. Built from then until 1986, these cars were generally referred to as 'Oscar India' cars, standing for 'October Introduction'. The most obvious differences were a re-styled bonnet and a swept up tail, while inside the cabin there was a re-designed dashboard and centre console, and the headlining became leather rather than cloth. There were other improvements, most notably to the air conditioning and shock absorber settings. :: 144 :: <BR/> :: 145 :: <BR/> :: 146 :: More History of the Aston Martin V8 :: 147 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/11 :: 148 :: <BR/> :: 149 :: <BR/> :: 150 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 151 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1981 Aston Martin V8 Volante for sale. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 134 :: 	<BR/> :: 135 :: Some History of the Aston Martin V8 :: 136 :: Shortly after re-organisation under new ownership as AML (1975) Ltd., Aston Martin resumed development of its highly successful V8. A host of improvements were to be incorporated in the forthcoming Series 4, scheduled for introduction in October 1978. Built from then until 1986, these cars were generally referred to as 'Oscar India' cars, standing for 'October Introduction'. The most obvious differences were a re-styled bonnet and a swept up tail, while inside the cabin there was a re-designed dashboard and centre console, and the headlining became leather rather than cloth. :: 137 :: <BR/> :: 138 :: <BR/> :: 139 :: More History of the Aston Martin V8 :: 140 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/11 :: 141 :: <BR/> :: 142 :: <BR/> :: 143 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 144 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1980 Aston Martin V8 Volante for sale. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 140 :: 	<BR/> :: 141 :: Some History of the Aston Martin DB7 :: 142 :: The Volante was launched to its biggest potential market in January 1996 at the Los Angeles and Detroit Motor Shows, at the same time as the Coupe. Capable of 161 mph, 60 mph in 5.8 seconds and 100 mph in a mere 14.4 seconds, the DB7 is no slouch, with 335 bhp at 5,600 rpm delivered via a 5-speed manual Getrag gearbox. :: 143 :: <BR/> :: 144 :: <BR/> :: 145 :: Widely recognised as one of the most beautiful and timeless design peices ever to feature in the automotive world, the Aston Martin DB7 was penned by Ian Callum and was availible in both coupe and convertible grand-tourer variants. Originally intended to replace the Aston Martin V8 Virage, which had recently suffered slow sales at Aston Martin dealers, the DB7 was based largely on the Jaguar XJS with which it shared its platform. The DB7 sold better than the flailing V8, moving out of the dealers swiftly before becoming the best selling Aston Martin ever. :: 146 :: <BR/> :: 147 :: <BR/> :: 148 :: More History of the Aston Martin DB7 :: 149 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/137 :: 150 :: <BR/> :: 151 :: <BR/> :: 152 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 153 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 2002 Aston Martin DB7 Volante for sale. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 138 :: 	<BR/> :: 139 :: Some History of the Lotus Elan :: 140 :: The Elans engine was a highly modified 1,498cc (later 1,558cc) Ford Cortina unit incorporating Lotuss own twin-camshaft cylinder head, and both the gearbox and differential came also from Ford. With the introduction of the improved S3 model in September 1965, the Elan became available as a fixed-head coup for the first time, having previously been sold only in drophead form with optional separate hardtop. Other civilising improvements included electric windows, re-designed dashboard and better trim. Powerful, light in weight and endowed with exceptional roadholding and handling, the Elan proved an immense commercial success for Lotus, slightly fewer than 9,000 being produced by the time production ceased in 1973.. :: 141 :: <BR/> :: 142 :: <BR/> :: 143 :: More History of the Lotus Elan :: 144 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/152 :: 145 :: <BR/> :: 146 :: <BR/> :: 147 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 148 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1969 Lotus Elan +2 S for sale. as 'a precision motorcar, an engineering tour de force', and it enjoyed a well deserved sales success. :: 142 :: <BR/> :: 143 :: <BR/> :: 144 :: Designed to replace the Lancia Appia and borrowing its engineering heavily from the Lancia Flavia, the Fulvia featured a newly designed narrow-angle V4 engine, independent suspension and all-round disc brakes. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 181 :: 	<BR/> :: 182 :: Some History of the Lotus Elan :: 183 :: Suspension was all independent with unequal-length wishbones at the front, while a wide-based lower wishbone and modified Chapman Strut, as used in Lotus Grand Prix cars, was employed at the rear. Rack-and-pinion steering was sourced from the Triumph Vitesse, and there were Girling disc brakes all round. The Elans engine was a highly modified 1,498cc (later 1,558cc) Ford Cortina unit incorporating Lotuss own twin-camshaft cylinder head, and both the gearbox and differential came also from Ford. With the introduction of the improved S3 model in September 1965, the Elan became available as a fixed-head coup for the first time, having previously been sold only in drophead form with optional separate hardtop. :: 184 :: <BR/> :: 185 :: <BR/> :: 186 :: More History of the Lotus Elan :: 187 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/152 :: 188 :: <BR/> :: 189 :: <BR/> :: 190 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 191 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1964 Lotus Elan 26R Clone for sale. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 141 :: 	<BR/> :: 142 :: Some History of the Aston Martin V8 :: 143 :: A host of improvements were to be incorporated in the forthcoming Series 4, scheduled for introduction in October 1978. Built from then until 1986, these cars were generally referred to as 'Oscar India' cars, standing for 'October Introduction'. The most obvious differences were a re-styled bonnet and a swept up tail, while inside the cabin there was a re-designed dashboard and centre console, and the headlining became leather rather than cloth. There were other improvements, most notably to the air conditioning and shock absorber settings. :: 144 :: <BR/> :: 145 :: <BR/> :: 146 :: More History of the Aston Martin V8 :: 147 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/11 :: 148 :: <BR/> :: 149 :: <BR/> :: 150 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 151 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1987 Aston Martin V8 Volante for sale. The Type M100 from 1989 to 1995, is also commonly known as the 1990s Elan. :: 65 :: <BR/> :: 66 :: The original Elan was introduced in 1962 as a roadster, although an optional hardtop was offered in 1963 and a coupé version in 1965. At 1,295 lb (585 kg), the Elan embodied the Colin Chapman minimum weight design philosophy. Initial versions of the Elan were also available as a kit to be assembled by the customer. The Elan was technologically advanced with a twin-cam 1558 cc engine, 4-wheel disc brakes, and 4-wheel independent suspension. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 180 :: 	<BR/> :: 181 :: Some History of the Lotus Elan :: 182 :: Suspension was all independent with unequal-length wishbones at the front, while a wide-based lower wishbone and modified Chapman Strut, as used in Lotus Grand Prix cars, was employed at the rear. Rack-and-pinion steering was sourced from the Triumph Vitesse, and there were Girling disc brakes all round. The Elans engine was a highly modified 1,498cc (later 1,558cc) Ford Cortina unit incorporating Lotuss own twin-camshaft cylinder head, and both the gearbox and differential came also from Ford. With the introduction of the improved S3 model in September 1965, the Elan became available as a fixed-head coup for the first time, having previously been sold only in drophead form with optional separate hardtop. :: 183 :: <BR/> :: 184 :: <BR/> :: 185 :: More History of the Lotus Elan :: 186 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/152 :: 187 :: <BR/> :: 188 :: <BR/> :: 189 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 190 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1964 Lotus Elan Series 1 1600 for sale. 	http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/rc.php/car/car%20data%20checks :: 140 :: 	<BR/> :: 141 :: Some History of the Lancia Aprilia :: 142 :: Vincenzo Lancias final great masterpiece was the Aprilia which went into production early in 1937, a new compact car, seating five in comfort and combining speed with economy. The aerodynamic saloon was of unitary construction with minimal (for the period) drag factor, sliding pillar front suspension, trailing arm rear suspension incorporating a transverse leaf spring, and powered by a forward mounted 1,352cc V4 engine. The all-new engine featured hemispherical combustion chambers, aluminium cylinder block and Duralumin conrods and developed some 47.8bhp. Designer Falchetto was responsible for the styling, with considerable influence from Pininfarina at Corso Trapani.. :: 143 :: <BR/> :: 144 :: <BR/> :: 145 :: More History of the Lancia Aprilia :: 146 :: http://www.classiccarsforsale.co.uk/classic-car-marques.php/marque/127 :: 147 :: <BR/> :: 148 :: <BR/> :: 149 :: 	Similar Cars For Sale :: 150 :: 	The classic cars for sale below are the cars we believe to be most similar to the featured 1939 Lancia Aprilia Pillarless Saloon for sale.
